RX   PubMed=17924946; DOI=10.1111/j.1365-2958.2007.05953.x;
RA   Seiboth B., Gamauf C., Pail M., Hartl L., Kubicek C.P.;
RT   "The D-xylose reductase of Hypocrea jecorina is the major aldose
RT   reductase in pentose and D-galactose catabolism and necessary for
RT   beta-galactosidase and cellulase induction by lactose.";
RL   Mol. Microbiol. 66:890-900(2007).
CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes the initial reaction in the xylose utilization
CC       pathway by reducing D-xylose into xylitol. Xylose is a major
CC       component of hemicelluloses such as xylan. Most fungi utilize D-
CC       xylose via three enzymatic reactions, xylose reductase (XR),
CC       xylitol dehydrogenase (XDH), and xylulokinase, to form xylulose 5-
CC       phosphate, which enters pentose phosphate pathway. Also major
CC       aldose reductase in pentose and D-galactose catabolism. Reduces
CC       the pentose L-arabinose and the hexose D-galactose to their
CC       respective polyols. Responsible for extracellular beta-
CC       galactosidase formation and cellulase induction during growth on
CC       lactose.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Alditol + NAD(P)(+) = aldose + NAD(P)H.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Xylitol + NAD(P)(+) = D-xylose + NAD(P)H.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946}.
CC   -!- BIOPHYSICOCHEMICAL PROPERTIES:
CC       Kinetic parameters:
CC         KM=25 mM for D-xylose {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=24 mM for D-ribose {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=41 mM for L-arabinose {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=82 mM for D-galactose {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=366 mM for D-glucose {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=11 mM for xylitol {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=76 mM for L-arabinitol {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=155 mM for galactitol {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=98 mM for ribitol {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=159 mM for D-sorbitol {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=0.023 mM for NADPH {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         KM=0.26 mM for NADH {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=176 nmol/sec/mg enzyme toward NADPH
CC         {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=0.42 nmol/sec/mg enzyme toward NADH
CC         {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=225 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with D-xylose as substrate for the
CC         reverse reaction {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=9 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with xylitol as substrate for the
CC         forward reaction {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=125 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with ribose as substrate for the
CC         reverse reaction {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=9 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with ribitol as substrate for the
CC         forward reaction {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=175 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with L-arabinose as substrate for
CC         the reverse reaction {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=16 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with L-arabinitol as substrate for
CC         the forward reaction {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=18 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with D-galactose as substrate for the
CC         reverse reaction {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=9 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with galactitol as substrate for the
CC         forward reaction {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=66 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with D-glucose as substrate for the
CC         reverse reaction {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC         Vmax=18 nmol/sec/mg enzyme with D-sorbitol as substrate for the
CC         forward reaction {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946};
CC   -!- PATHWAY: Carbohydrate metabolism; D-xylose degradation.
CC   -!- PATHWAY: Carbohydrate degradation; L-arabinose degradation via L-
CC       arabinitol; D-xylulose 5-phosphate from L-arabinose (fungal
CC       route): step 1/5.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Regulated by carbon source. Most abundant during growth
CC       on D-xylose and L-arabinose. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:17924946}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the aldo/keto reductase family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes the initial reaction in the xylose utilization
CC       pathway by reducing D-xylose into xylitol. Xylose is a major
CC       component of hemicelluloses such as xylan. Most fungi utilize D-
CC       xylose via three enzymatic reactions, xylose reductase (XR),
CC       xylitol dehydrogenase (XDH), and xylulokinase, to form xylulose 5-
CC       phosphate, which enters pentose phosphate pathway (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Xylitol + NAD(P)(+) = D-xylose + NAD(P)H.
CC   -!- PATHWAY: Carbohydrate metabolism; D-xylose degradation.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the aldo/keto reductase family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes the initial reaction in the xylose utilization
CC       pathway by reducing D-xylose into xylitol. Xylose is a major
CC       component of hemicelluloses such as xylan. Most fungi utilize D-
CC       xylose via three enzymatic reactions, xylose reductase (XR),
CC       xylitol dehydrogenase (XDH), and xylulokinase, to form xylulose 5-
CC       phosphate, which enters pentose phosphate pathway (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Catalyzes the initial reaction in the xylose utilization
CC       pathway by reducing D-xylose into xylitol. Xylose is a major
CC       component of hemicelluloses such as xylan. Most fungi utilize D-
CC       xylose via three enzymatic reactions, xylose reductase (XR),
CC       xylitol dehydrogenase (XDH), and xylulokinase, to form xylulose 5-
CC       phosphate, which enters pentose phosphate pathway (By similarity).
CC       {ECO:0000250}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Xylitol + NAD(P)(+) = D-xylose + NAD(P)H.
CC   -!- PATHWAY: Carbohydrate metabolism; D-xylose degradation.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Overexpressed during growth on both D-xylose or L-
CC       arabinose compared to D-glucose. Significantly expressed during
CC       late stages of infection of barley leaves.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:23499935}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the aldo/keto reductase family.
CC       {ECO:0000305}.

CC   -!- FUNCTION: Endo-1,4-beta-xylanase involved in the hydrolysis of
CC       xylan, a major structural heterogeneous polysaccharide found in
CC       plant biomass representing the second most abundant polysaccharide
CC       in the biosphere, after cellulose. Accounts for approximately 70
CC       percent of the endoxylanase activity in the culture filtrate.
CC       {ECO:0000269|Ref.2}.
CC   -!- CATALYTIC ACTIVITY: Endohydrolysis of (1->4)-beta-D-xylosidic
CC       linkages in xylans. {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8589407}.
CC   -!- PATHWAY: Glycan degradation; xylan degradation.
CC   -!- SUBCELLULAR LOCATION: Secreted {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8589407}.
CC   -!- INDUCTION: Expressed in presence of rice cell walls or on oat
CC       spelt xylan, but not when grown on sucrose.
CC       {ECO:0000269|PubMed:8589407}.
CC   -!- DISRUPTION PHENOTYPE: Retains 39 percent of the catalytic
CC       activity. Double xyl1/xyl2 deletion mutant retains 19 percent of
CC       the activity and exhibits a 50 percent reduction in accumulation
CC       of total mycelial mass. {ECO:0000269|Ref.2}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Belongs to the glycosyl hydrolase 10 (cellulase F)
CC       family. {ECO:0000305}.
CC   -!- SIMILARITY: Contains 1 GH10 (glycosyl hydrolase family 10) domain.
CC       {ECO:0000255|PROSITE-ProRule:PRU01096}.
